> [Quoting gerval](/thread/post/14403773#post14403773 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hi nadi-fx, thanks for sharing. EURUSD alone or does it also use more pairs? I understand that he uses any level marked on the chart to enter if he is given a 1:3. It looks Interesting and a good time stamp to not spend all day in front of the screen.
> 
> Ignored

Hi Gerval. Yes only e/u for several reason.  
1\. Because of using tight stop (30pips) so less wild wired moves, less stop hunting.  
2\. Reliability, 40% of all currency volume is on this pair, moves are meaningful.  
3\. Less screen time, checking on one pair vs several or more.  
4\. Most pairs are correlated on longer time frame anyways and dollar driven, so instead of splitting the load on serval or more pairs why not put it all on the most reliable and meaningful one.. less to watchdog.  
  
I hope it helps. 

Stay the Course

I see a few squares and lines, how do they differentiate?

  * Apr 24, 2023 4:21pm  Apr 24, 2023 4:21pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting TDT.Coffee](/thread/post/14403979#post14403979 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Great Thread Nadi! Based on your first Post I can tell that you are a very experienced trader. Everyone who visits this thread should take this guy serious and learn from his Charts! ____________ Could you elaborate more on how you draw your Zones? I see a few squares and lines, how do they differentiate? Your lines are sometimes neither on the body nor on the bottom of the wick. Are the lines exactly where you want to enter, or do they just visually show where you generally want to enter (around this area). What if your desired 3R TP doesnt make...
> 
> Ignored

Hi friend and thanks for kind words.  
Getting ready to go to bed but I will answer this one.  
  
Good observation on the LV lines. I don't use zones. I draw the lines based on the length of the wick and trade right at that level point bcz of my tight stops (30) I got to be precise and consistent to create discipline.  
So, if the length of the wick is small to mediocre (2 to 10pips) I draw the line on the middle of it. If its large like 20 pips I draw it at 2/3 and if very large I draw it inside 10 pips. I cannot be too far from the peak, because there is always a chance of retest of the very peak and some before the bounce, so need to give myself the extra 20 pips from the peak to my stop level. However you will miss triggers by a few pips off or stops to be hit by a few pips bcz LV was off a bit and that's just part of the game. All I can do is to follow the same structure for proven consistent results to go by.  
  
about profit taking on levels.. no level is important nor unimportant I treat them all the same.. I only pay attention to how jammed they are. if its not giving me the 3R I initially have the target at next level but if i see price is reacting to this mediocre level and not breaking through it then i just bank, but i give it a chance to break it. for example on the current short trade i got my tp at bottom level and not at the immediate one that is about 70 pips.  
  
The small squares are the entries. just for my notes.  
  
about position taking.. the target has nothing to do with me taking up on a level. I trade all levels bcz at any level price can bounce and take off is mass and I hate to not be on that bus.  
  
I hope it helps  
GL. 

Stay the Course

> [Quoting gerval](/thread/post/14404518#post14404518 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Reading the thread I saw that an operation like the one he took was prepared, this time SL. Prepared the following levels and testing in demo. It treats the levels the same, sl and tp whether or not there is a trend?, as in the current case. One last thing, because of the translator I did not understand correctly, when the price goes in your favor, 30 pips move to BE and let the operation develop? {image}
> 
> Ignored

Yes, so when you place you limit order you also put in a 30 pips trail stops. That means when price goes in your favor for 30 pips the SL moves to Breakeven (BE) and then you remove the Trail stop.   
I do not trail stop my position I just do the one-time trail stop to BE and that's it. I secure a no loss after been rewarded with some leeway.  
  
I hope it helps.  
GL 

Stay the Course

10695 LV is the next one likely to be triggered with sell limit. 30pips hard stop in place the 30 pips one time trail in place and target I put it between the two jammed levels for about +140 I will exit that trade no matter what at that point, it's a good enough profit what my plan and goal I can care or less if this drops in mass.  
just thinking ahead of time based on structure and plan.. that level could get run through and shoot up to the moon and take me for 30, np... or yet worse, it could fake out for 40 hit my 30 stops then runs down, lol... it's all part of the game.  
you look at my chart and see some of the trades are look to be absurd and say to yourself well i can avoid those its too obvious!! ok.. you do that and you will lose out on big gains from the tiniest unimportant levels for sure hands down. you will have price coming at your sell limit with so much heat lets say after some major news and most if not all of you will remove that limit order bcz you think it will for sure run though it or to at least hit your tight stops of 30.. but only to watch and witness one of the best bounces of your life (eg, 2nd chart)  
So, I don't know, all I can do is to watch my behind.   
Risk Management,  
Capital Preservation,  
Patience  
Following structures...  
  
Thats your edge.

> Hi nadi, When determining your levels, do you use any sort of trendline breaks to filter out the mediocre levels? I assume they are mediocre because they fall between a high and low levels? thx {quote}
> 
> Ignored

Hi Dave,   
No, no trend lines... throughout my career I have tried to stay away from trend lines bcz they are hard to draw and are controversial, I could never find a solid structure for it that I can rely on... they just look sexy after the fact IMHO.  
Mid-levels are smaller V's or less data less volume that's why they may not be as strong or reliable... I have no problem with mid-levels they payoff well too.  
Instead of filtering I manage risk and stay true to my tight stops.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

  * [#28](/thread/post/14407203#post14407203 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 1:47am  Apr 27, 2023 12:45am | Edited 1:47am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

The way Price is reacting around the 10620 level is a very good lesson for the thread followers. Most times you will get a clean bounce, or a clean stop hit. But there are times when price plays around at the level like what we are witnessing now.. it gave us a false break out and hoovering around the level still as to not sure if it's going to head down or resume the bull run or go circles.  
so usually at this time I just sit on my hands and at least wait to see how the H4 candle closes if I have to take another shot at it going short, it has sting me already once. This level now is a suspect and a suspicious one... more time will reveal its hand, and if it run short now me not in it, it's fine bcz I already took a shot at it and can't do much about fake outs, it's part of the game. A guy told me once, "you atta make out with fake out" lol ... it will happen, be ok with it.  
The point I am trying to hit home is;  
To not start wondering  
To not start messing around with Stops level (move it from 30-40 or 50 or extended to next level etc)  
To question everything just bcz one level or handful of levels behave this way... be ok with the loss and the deceive... this market is a beast.  
... stay the course  
  
I am not lecturing by no means... just giving insight of what I do and go about it based on my own hard-fought experience throughout years.  
I also know and understand why there isn't enough followers so no need to lecture much but for a few that are here this prime live example should work out well and I couldn't hold back. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

If there was bad luck with the short entry and the SL for two pips and it is still in the green... it means that when it develops normally and in the long term it will compensate you.

> [Quoting ozziedave](/thread/post/14407518#post14407518 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Are you taking into account any trend basis or strickly trading level to level no matter what the overall trend is?
> 
> Ignored

No matter what the trend is Price still plays level to level most times!!... as we all got to know that no price goes straight up or down... pullbacks are a given and resumes are a possibility, so with level to level you could easily fall into trends automatically at the luxury of double tops/bottoms.  
So, I have eliminated the stress of trend or no trend off my trading style and take things at face value to test the market at peaks and valleys where money was either inserted In or Out, some are strong some are not and meant to be broken resume trend or held tight to bounce to start a whole new move which I am in it from the very beginning where it creates lots of room for me to may let it ride and enjoy the also so called trend for more than my 3R goal.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL

  * [#40](/thread/post/14408400#post14408400 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 28, 2023 12:49am  Apr 28, 2023 12:49am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting nguyenoni](/thread/post/14407885#post14407885 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Bro! i have an question, how do you detect and draw the zone buy or sell limit in the chart? Are you using MACD histogram to detect top or bottom in H4 timeframe? Thankyou so much!
> 
> Ignored

The MacD has nothing to do with my trading bcz is super lagging like every other indicator... it's just a visual for after the fact that there was a peak or valley after i have already taken action on it. When you trade with limit orders you are ahead of all indicators! meaning you are not waiting for confirmations to do xyz. That is why you see zero indicators on my chart.  
About drawing the lines i have explained it in first a few posts I think please refer there. But in short no Zones... need to draw the line precise and trade right at that. You could use zones too but its not a clear discipline structure, your stop hit will be affected when you use zone unless increase the stop level to much higher like 60 from 30... now you are looking at a totally different ball game.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

> Disliked
> 
> I am confused. Is it not sell limit on HH and buy limit on LL ?
> 
> Ignored

its right you got it... on HH or peaks you use sell limit and on LL or valleys you use buy limits.   
you are basically counter trading when taking action on bounces so when price is going up you sell and going down you buy.  
  
GL

  * [#43](/thread/post/14408447#post14408447 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:13am  Apr 28, 2023 1:56am | Edited 2:13am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

I wanna show you guys something, just my humble take...  
Since the Trend issue has arisen which was a given, very common one and an important one, so I address it with example, so you all know where I am coming from.  
  
Look at the first chart which is the weekly chart. We had one of the longest lasting bear trends in E/U in recent times. It lasted 15 months, that's 60 weeks for total of 27Cents or 2700 pips. The overall trend has been bearish (dollar strong) since 2008... leg down in 2008 another leg down 2014 and this last one as I just pointed out.  
now back to the example... if I had a crystal ball, I would have made one sell trade and keep it for 2700 pips! one clean position stress free paying less fees less to none screen time letting that baby ride to make banks right at the end of it for 2700pips, just beautiful... but I don't, nor will I need it or want it to be honest with you... bcz I can make more through Peaks and Valleys without the complications of trends and duration of it... not to mention trading is my passion and I want to be more engaged. I love getting up in the morning be excited to check my charts making adjustment reading articles etc before heading to real life work and business.  
I should also mention that position trading is very profitable, but it is for big institutions, and we are just little retail traders with much much smaller accounts. That is a different ball game.  
okey, as I was saying that trend lasted for 60 weeks... even if I make 50pips a week I can beat 2700 pips and had to never worry or stress about what overall trend was is or doing. Spotting a trend _beforehand and lasting in it_ is very difficult, stressful, unpredictable and you name it.  
Now look at the next chart. I mentioned in the initial first post the expectation and goal are to make 100pips a week, some weeks you will some don't but in the end, it all averages out if you stick to the plan and stay the course. So, in the 2nd chart you see how simply you will make way more than 100 pips in any given week to make up for loss weeks or no gain weeks. If you scroll though the past you will see good solid weeks where in 200 pips overall weeks of movement you have managed to make 200 or even 300 pips just bouncing up and down or catch a nice little runner on the jammed space when it breaks out with your target at a next level to be... in feature we will see those live, I hope.  
60 weeks' time times 100 pips are 6000 pips, and I could care or less about market trend. I rather bank on the obvious... historically market sideways 2/3 of times than it trends and pullbacks are given, price cannot not go straight up or down, period. Those are facts that I can rely and bank on.  
  
I hope it makes sense and if it does not, I can understand... this is just my humble way of thinking and trading the market... hence I don't downplay or eliminate trend completely out of my trading its just not priority if I fall into it great if not it is not the core of what i do.  
  
Now, the trend advocates, please don't beat me down, I don't want any part of it you win, and I respect your opinions, market knowledge hands down. ![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44d.png?v=15.1)  
  
In trading you should know YOU, that's your real edge. I know me that I am incapable of Predicting the market... incapable of complications... but capable of simplicity, structures. I try to do my best to follow my plan as I have learned to earn from this market, and I should say, humbly for now... this is a beast that we are dealing with, never doubt that.  
  
GL

  * [#62](/thread/post/14409944#post14409944 "Post Permalink")

  * Apr 29, 2023 2:00am  Apr 29, 2023 2:00am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting mdz4h5](/thread/post/14409931#post14409931 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Do you keep positions open over the weekend?
> 
> Ignored

Good question.  
I try not to. Most times I close it. Like this buy trade that I am in... if the target is not hit and its hanging around +70 pips or so I would just bank it and call the week.  
However, if ever i was lucky enough to fall into a trend that I am in significant gains like 200 pips and going on a strong PA, in such rare case I would secure +100 and let it ride over the weekend with plenty of room to not be affected by Gap action.  
  
The main reason for not leaving positions open over the weekend is to not risk your account. If a financial Armageddon happens your stops will not be honored, and you could lose your whole account (could get massive gain too)... so not wise to risk that.  
  
Therefore its better off to close all position remove all orders keep the account free and clear. I have alert set for hour before the Friday close to assess the situation to do so.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

Clean chart the buy position closed an hour before market close good for +55 and all other orders removed.

The real dagger for me was missing the sell trade by 2 pips... also, two stops being hit by 1-2 pips didn't help either otherwise I would have had a monster week. Thats the way it goes at times.  
Missing the first sell trade was totally my mistake as i did not draw my line correctly off by 4pips or so.  
  
Just the little summary of the week behind us.

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting Dariusfxlife](/thread/post/14410298#post14410298 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Thanks for sharing your trading style and the details on how you approach the market. Your focus on risk management and sticking to a plan with discipline is a valuable reminder for all traders. One question: How do you determine your trade size for the upcoming weeks based on your available equity?
> 
> Ignored

Yes, based on available equity risking 1-2%.  
  
$1500 x 2% = $30 / 30 pips SL = $1 per pips  
  
Accounts 50K under risk 2%... 50K+ risking 1% (recommendation)  
  
GL  
  
ps) I must add, when we talk equity, you must assess that safely. Equity is floating! Meaning your open positions could go against you and you must know what the worst-case scenario is and calculate your risk accordingly.  
Otherwise just go based on Balance.

> Disliked
> 
> Hi thanks for your thread. A couple of questions if I may. Do you drop down into smaller time frames when looking to exit a trade or are you strongly disciplined to remain on H4? Do you ever have multiple positions open and if so does this come about by adding market orders or do you place limit orders again? Thanks
> 
> Ignored

Hi ax,   
No, I never drop down if anything I look up to D1. Anything under H4 is noise to me.  
I hardly ever have multiple open positions... if I ever do is on two instances;  
1) When I am on hedge... meaning I decided to not exit at a level looking for more profit but at the same time been triggered at that level in opposite way, bcz I still will test the level.  
2) I could be in some trades in heavy profit for 1/10 the load... for eg, I have banked 90% and just let 10% run for however long it maybe.  
This is something I was going to get into in this thread when the opportunity arrived.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

Here are the levels for this week I got five limit order going to start it al off.  
The whole range inside this sideway action is 190pips. If PA plays inside the box, you will make money... if it breaks out, you will be hit with some stops but might be riding in on a breaking out. targets if you choose to set one should be on top and bottom to get 3R+... for now I have left it alone to not crowed the chart also might give the PA the chance to break out one for me to enjoy a bit of a trend money, who knows.  
Most importantly you don't wanna miss a ride and for that you need to test the market at these levels.  
gotta be in it to win it lol.  
  
I highly welcome you to share your chart.  
  
Best of luck to all for this week's trading.

Recommendation;  
I have my phone alarm set to check the chart every 4hrs on start of every H4 candle.  
At my time zone west coast time it goes like this... 2PM market open and close, 6pm,10pm... 2am off bcz i am sleep and don't wanna be bothered at no cost.. 6am, 10am.  
5-10min spent on the chart if I have to make adjustments but more importantly to just be engaged with what's going on.

> 
> Disliked
> 
> Morning I did not see this anywhere in the thread so sorry if I just missed it. NEWS red flag I am assuming you just let price do its own thing. But do you make exceptions for Interest rates announcements. or Non Fam. Regards martin
> 
> Ignored

Morning, good question.  
I don't put too much weight on news bcz I am on higher TF and won't fall victim to whiplash as much as the lower tf do.  
However, on the major ones like NFP and Rates if I have too many jammed up orders on levels close to the price before such news releases, I just make sure the closest one is at least 50-70+ pips away.  
for example, this week we have the nfp & FOMC and we are in a tight range, let's say price stays still at where it is I will remove the in between order and take my chances with tops and bottoms only. That would be 9117 and 10835.  
Overall, I personally not too concerned about any news... my risk is plenty wise and all such stops hit is all pre accounted. at times I give up a 30-40 (on whiplash your SL will be more bcz of speed on the price or gap at times) in seconds when price just runs through it and other times, I get a nice bounce for major gains and possibly fall into a deep trend.  
I recommend to for thread and inexperience, to sit on your hands at such major news till feel more confident.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

  * [#87](/thread/post/14411689#post14411689 "Post Permalink")

  * May 2, 2023 12:43am  May 2, 2023 12:43am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

The buy trade above is good example of staying the course.  
Some of you might pass on this when you see price coming at you with 70 pips straight heat!! or say lets wait and see how it reacts around it to not get in with limit, too risky.   
Sure, it might work this time or some other time, but bounces happen really fast, and you end up either missing the trade or getting in late out of place to risk stop hit... or yet worse add length to the stop to cover the HH LL possibility of losing more, which will affect the bottom-line.  
  
See, I eliminate all that stress and just let it play out... my risk is predetermined, and I am good with it.  
I cannot miss the bus.  
  
Just a little humble take on mental stuff.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

As I pointed out in the chart... a lot of activities on those bounces where new money was inserted and finally gave in to the bulls.  
That is even more of a reason why I stand ground on my levels and limit order, even when price approaches it with lots of heat, 70pips full bold H4 candle.  
... is valid till crushed lol...  
however, most if not all levels are meant to be broken at some point and time, it's just a matter of how profitable it was before it breaks out.  
  
  
GL

  * Edited 6:08am  May 2, 2023 4:27am | Edited 6:08am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

Guys do not draw your LV on any TF other than H4. The LV's are based on high tf... on lower tf you will have whole bunch more levels, less reliable. D1 is too far out and conservative and H1 and under too much noise, go with the middle which is H4.  
Train yourself to stick to one TF when choosing your Levels.  
  
Just my humble take. 

Stay the Course

...offense is first defense second. Nothing matters is continuously keep getting kick out of winners.

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [1 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#102](/thread/post/14412212#post14412212 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 4:59pm  May 2, 2023 3:07pm | Edited 4:59pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting Seabreeze](/thread/post/14412204#post14412204 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> Hello nadi-fx Great thread and following with interest. The latest buy trade you entered at 9704 can you highlight where your take profit is so I can compare if I have it right. Still learning this but not 100% sure whether you religious have a 3-1 Risk to reward or take profit at the next level regardless if risk reward. Thank you for your time.
> 
> Ignored

Hi, my take profit on this trade is already set up top at 10750 about 100pips. I initially always shoot for 3R especially if it falls into a solid level, I bank it like where I have for this buy trade. However, there is a level before that at 10388ish around 70 pips profit, If I see price not breaking it easily and plays around it, I could just take the 70 there. In another words I will not settle so easily for take profit when a level is lower than 3R or 90 pips and initially is set at following level.  
Nothing is set in stone, but I will stand my ground to get my 3Rs and wont panic or give up on littles threats.  
  
Overall, it's about having a structure and following it, but in a frame of managing risk too... many things to consider in different circumstances, such as;  
what day of the week I am,  
what kind of profit or loss I am at,  
am I excelling or bleeding,  
... and a few other factors... and then to act accordingly.  
  
I give you couple of scenarios...  
let's say it's Thursday week is winding down, I have had 3 trades all losses, so I am down 90 pips... I enter the 4th trade, it is not a loser but only a weak winner meaning its stuck at some mediocre level where it could easily turn on me and eat my profit. At this juncture its wise for me to bank a descent some if I can, let's say 65pips to reduce the bleeding, one more day in the week is left and I may not be able to survive such week... so I accept and walk away with my 25 pips loss for the week or a better opportunity later... keeping my head above the water.  
another one could be... its Wednesdays, been in couple of trade one win one loss and I am up +60... on following trade I will follow the structure fully and stay on offense aggressively to reach my 100pips avg goal and possibly beyond.  
The name of the game is to survive first and to go for the kill second... for me IMHO.  
  
In normal circumstances I follow my structure religiously to answer your question, let it play out the way it should.  
  
I hope it help and I answered it to best I could.  
  
GL

hi and thank you.  
The answer to this question is in my first post... but thread is young, and I'll answer it again.  
I filter with "Time", Two weeks. Recent levels! as you also mentioned. Recent to me is two weeks. Otherwise, you will have a level at every step of the price.  
If no reaction on a level after two weeks is dead to me, I don't care how strong once it was.  
so in short...  
* Two weeks with no rejection reaction  
* or... once is broken.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

> Disliked
> 
> Morning With regard to say a buy order running with a 90 pip TP above the entry. But we have a sell order at 70 pips above where we took the long would the sell order not negate and close the long position. I have never tried it so may be dependent on the broker used (IE if they operate order cancels order) Regards
> 
> Ignored

your fellow trader here name axecap asked similar question i have explained there, so please refer to post 104.  
but on extended explanation;  
I treat each trade as individually and at its own... so I could be in both trade going the opposite direction of each. if i am in buy then 70 pips later there is a level for sell, i take the sell and may leave the buy still open for more profit. this happens for most cases when my 3R has not meet. I stand ground for that.  
But if I have meet my 3R profit and then i got a level coming I bank and reverse. At no cost I will not let a new level trade opportunity to be wasted.  
  
Technically speaking... you will need to operate with a broker that allows hedge or no FIFO.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

Yes buddy it serves well most time but also stings you at times too when fakes you out one more time before taking off. But you wanna be more safe than sorry.  
on this one I was fortunate enough to notice the move before going to bed and manually move it to BE at 35 pips gain... if i am sleep my trail is set at 40.  
Overall that bounce was kind of weak from get go and I could expect this to not be a super star move.  
The one-time trail 30-40 pips serve well in the long run. The key is when you do get faked and kicked out before runs to the moon to _Not affect_ you and start change things around.  
Stay the course, it's all part of the game.

  * [#130](/thread/post/14414253#post14414253 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited May 4, 2023 12:10am  May 3, 2023 11:46pm | Edited May 4, 2023 12:10am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

Be prepared for two stops to be hit or be rewarded with a major gain, or to clear your chart and sit on your hands till dust settles, that is totally fine too. Only YOU are in charge of your risk management for your account. There is always pros and cons, risk reward. The difference is we keep our risk limited and our reward extended.  
One win clears at least 3 losses.  
As a retail trader who is at the mercy of secondhand info following the footsteps of price and not leading the price. There is a big difference there my friends, to follow and not lead. Therefore, 3R is my best friend... so when I do fall in-line with the big boys (1 in 3 times) I have to maximize. At least the way I trade.  
all in IMHO.  
  
I just wanted to throw that out there before wild time.  
  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

Now the best ideal situation to be on the buy trade that we had a massive bounce yesterday. I was super bum stunned how it missed me by hair. I wanted to be in driver sit for the major news coming up this week.  
This is how I would have played it out;  
today is sitting at 100+ pips cushion. I would set my take profit sitting at 50-60 pips or halfway and let that baby ride if its meant to go bull. Or, scale it by taking half off and letting it ride. By no means I would have liquidated the whole position. Because the reward could be massive at times after such news, and you could be sitting on a ride for long time.  
Now what that does for your bottom line is to wipe all or most of your stops hit or to be hit even if you have 2/10 of the position riding.  
Just something to keep in back of your mind for the next time.  
  
GL

In the case of both candles, the wick is longer than 20 pips. So my understanding is the 10 pips inward rule should apply. The low of 20th is 1.09380 and so limit should be at 1.09480 and also; the low of 21st is 1.09334 and so limit should be at 1.09433. I hope that I have the right understanding of what you kindly shared?...
> 
> Ignored

Jewel... that was the way I analyzed it. However, I was one of the fortunate who had their trade trigger... because in retrospect I wasn't 100% precise with the 10 pip rule... my entry was at 1.0943 rather than 1.09433. Hope that helps.

If no reaction on a level after two weeks is dead to me, I don't care how strong once it was. so in short... * Two weeks with no rejection reaction * or... once is broken. GL

  * Edited 2:48pm  May 7, 2023 8:47am | Edited 2:48pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

Week in review...  
We were blessed with five level to level trade opportunities to deal with in sideway action. FOMC/NFP week and no real breakout occurred... NFPs dust still is not settled tho, and that is why I kept my buy position open hoping for bullish continuation.  
Produced two winners +140/+80... one stop hit -30... one BE and one pending, in profit for 20 at zero risk as of now.  
Overall, a successful week with surpassing the weekly goal and beyond.  
However, as you all know some of us did not trigger on the buy trade and I was one of them. But still, managed to bank +50 for the week with an open buy position at +20 on zero risk. Hopefully shoots up so I can meet my weekly goal of 100 and plus.  
  
For the coming week we got 4 solid levels to place limit order, two extremes and two mid-range levels all clearly visible in the chart below.  
  
I thought people were more engaged, active, posing great questions, observing and some expressed concern and dismissal about the whole deal, which is all good and fine.  
The fact is forums belong to public, and everyone are surly the master of their own judgement for their own good as to beak who and what is right or benefits them to follow or unfollow. All that is good as long as agendas are purely to only serve good.  
I am only sharing not teaching technicals, everything in this market has been already taught and shared for million times. Everyone does it in their own taste, style, flair and some tweaking which might fall in-line and suitable with some others, to trade together in a peaceful community. All systems and methods etc after X's and O's, comes down to how well you manage risk consistently in a structural manner... and that is a never-ending process of learning, practice and executions in the heat of the battle.  
Respect is all I have asked for and kindly reminding it.  
  
Looking forward to the new week and positive results.  
  
GL

Keep posting as I find your trading approach interesting and you have a few nice fellow traders interested too. Hopefully we can keep a nice friendly thread going between us.  
  
Good luck to everyone this week.   
  
I like to prep my charts before looking at yours to see if I am getting it right. So far so good.

That is a minor level. That level was approached with a lot of heat from earlier bounce (the buy trade that I missed by a hair). on that on i treated as a one that wait & see how PA reacts to it which after a doji it shot up quickly. if it had hoovered around it for serval candles and I was able to get in at the right price up top I would have test it.   
There is a difference between testing a level at possible PAs exhaustion and at its peak. This was at its very peak.   
I don't do that often nor like it... I rather test and give up 30 to not mis a ride.

> {quote} If this current trade get to BE and drops, what is the next line of action: should there now be a sell limit at 0977ish or we wait for a swing low to be formed and then put a buy limit for when it returns. In the meantime we still keep the sell limits at 10486 and 10865. Have you ever had a loosing month with this strategy. If it had dropped with a real break out then yes that would have made that swing low a legit level to go short from, but now we notice is not and one maybe in the making a bit up top at 10000.  
Both sell limit are very much intact till two weeks filter takes them out.  
232 is in... good suggestion.  
  
Okey and now the main question; as I have been asked several times in different shape and form, so I will answer it once and for all and add it to first post.  
**"Have you ever had a losing month with this strategy?** " or etc in that nature.  
... sure, if and when I fuck up... if and when I try to outsmart the market and myself, get too wise for my own good... when I panic and let fear in to act desperate... when I become impatient with even results or mediocre results then fall off the pathway try to get too creative.  
but, when I stay even kill, stay the course, sticking to trading plan and style... ya, losing is far and away FOR ME.  
The fact is, I know my market philosophy and I trust it because I have sweat it out for many years of trading, and won't change it for the world, not based on ego but rather success... because is based on when and where Money was inserted and deserted, so, I test the market on those spots (peaks and valley, levels) to keep probability on my side with 3R+ hammer on top of it, for the possible lack of mediocre win rate. Keeping losses short, maximizing winners (30pips stops/BE, 3R+)  
  
folks, don't put much weight on any one to throw in bunch of personal stats for you on how successful they are or once were. instead, put weight on actual market sense and philosophy, a base, as to if it makes sense to you or not, is it market Savvy, is it based on some valuable market core or some xyz digital codes... more important of all, is it for you or not, does it fit your personality or not, does it fit your agenda and goals or not, is it at your speed or not.  
eg, even if I am a god trader, I would not be able to scalp for shit, bcz is just not me... I won't stare at charts for hours. Or short time trading or too long. Or too volatile crazy wild pair. Or high risky, high variance, and etc  
As a trader in my opinion, you got to be flexible adapt to what's successful and implement it, but at the same token it got to fit YOU.  
You will never get any number from me based on my results besides what you see in forward trading you witness here. My results have nothing to do with yours period.  
  
This post is for everybody, Thanks for the question, Jewel.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

the 2nd image I already explained to you... the origin is nothing but a wick in a continuation, there is no V there, otherwise every pullback is a V. there is no level formed there yet.. did we sell from there!! I have not even put a level there yet, let alone selling.   
a pullback and resume sets a level.  
you need to understand the difference between a wick and a push off or a wick with continuation.  
  
This is very simple my friend. please do the due diligent, with all due respect. if this is your thing read the 1st post and all other important posts a few times and study the chart for hours and hours.  
  
GL... bcz right now you need a lot of it, not to be harsh. 

Stay the Course

It starts with price pullbacks which will define valley to put a Buy limit then double top or N action to go short with sell limit.

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

Two recommendations;  
* Don't use indicators to define your levels, you will have lines everywhere crowds your chart way too much, keeps you out of touch... learn to train your eyes to see it yourself and draw it. Not to mention if you are following the thread most of levels from an indicator is filtered. so you be trading not based on what we do here.  
* Don't go below H4 timeframe. Its noise and you have to watch dog the chart every 15 min or hour. again, that's not what we do here.  
and if I have to use one more recommendation that would be to ignore post 262, with all due respect.  
  
But it's all entirely up to you.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

Goodmorning, so the none signal sell trade did not work out but I lost only 12 pips on that one moved the stops up before going to bed after a little cushion it gave.  
overall, a dumb trade not within the plan but I was up +40 and this probably was the only chance to get me back to my weekly goal... still finishing the week with +30.  
I consider this week a survival one... trades were against market will and that's when power of 3R comes handy, one win covers 3 losses, with 25%-win rate you breakeven.  
I am done for the week all orders removed.  
  
Week is winding down, market heading south, dollar strengthening, bracket broken and will see how it shapes up. for now, no buy limits, sell limits far and away.  
what's next! price will halt makes a pullback and you get yourself a Valley that's a level to go long... after pullback it may resume, and the resume point becomes your peak that's a level to go short on next visit (double top) that's how you will get in this bear move. 9310 is the closest to it atm.  
  
Possible scenarios;  
* Price pulls back and gets stuck in a sideway action you will make ton of money.  
* Price pulls back but gets in choppy action, you will BE for most parts.  
* Price pulls back gives you double top and shoots down you will make money and possibly continue to stay in the trend, (next phase I will show you, if still here)  
* Price pulls back and resumes and breaks the valley hard every time you will lose 30 every time... but if shows slightest reaction/bounce you still might get away with BE results at times.  
so, that's the way it goes.  
  
one thing is for certain, price will halt, price will pullback... and markets overall sideways 2/3 of times. Based on those facts I know I can make money and not lose money, IF I can keep myself in check. So, it comes down to YOU.  
  
Have a wonderful weekend folks.

  * Edited 8:07am  May 14, 2023 4:52am | Edited 8:07am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

> [Quoting Jewel1996](/thread/post/14424908#post14424908 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> if its not giving me the 3R I initially have the target at next level but if i see price is reacting to this mediocre level and not breaking through it then i just bank, but i give it a chance to break it. for example on the current short trade i got my tp at bottom level and not at the immediate one that is about 70 pips. Please do you have specific price action strategy to determine if price is reacting to or breaking a mediocre level? Do you sometimes go down to the lower time frames eg H1 to see this reactions? I guess it may also help to explain...
> 
> Ignored

I never go to lower time frame if anything I go up.  
No specific PA strategy... it either breaks the level hard or reacts to it with a hesitation or bounce. I will at times give it the chance for the hard break, that's all.  
Now...  
1\. If level is short of my 3R, I hold for the break to bank at next level for 3R. (Like on the buy trade this past week)  
2\. If level satisfies 3Rs but it's in a sideway action I bank at the quickest hesitation. (like the sell trade mid this week for 103)  
3\. If level is in the trending mood PA stepping, I will be more tolerable, take the hard break more seriously to maximize on possible trend.  
... the 3rd scenario is something we have not seen yet but PA looks to be trending bear now... so if we are able to get on this on a pullback double top.. we will look for bottom hard break for trend continuation. (chart below)  
The probability is higher on trending PA for continuation level to be broken, especially early stages of the Trend.  
It's just all commonsense to me more than anything else instead of PA predicting, reading etc,... trend can stop at any time... we just won't know. But there are early stages when its ripe and exhaustion time when near winding down... both are very visible in the charts.  
Now, all of that depends on my Risk Management too... where I am at that time of the week... down two stops, even, up, killing it etc  
Trading is not all clean cut... it's all about the buck in the end more than the Xs and Os.  
  
I hope it helps.  
  
GL

90% of times when price breaks the Level hard your stop is hit... but when it does not and resumes back in your favor it can turn into a winner or breakeven... like the sell trade we had late last week (red circle).. I end up BE that one but some of you even banked 30-40 pips.  
stop survived a hard break on that one, which traveled about 26 pips.

I see again and very eagerly we have another Level indicator posted here.  
As I said before, learn to train your eyes to see it yourself and to draw it yourself and not depend on xyz to all that for you. This way you be more engaged with price and chart, builds muscle memory, becomes second nature.  
Level that is broken is dead and that is what this whatever indicator or most other don't show and therefore your chart is full of lines, just be aware of which one to filter if you chose to not listen to me and want to use it.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

  * May 16, 2023 1:57am  May 16, 2023 1:57am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

Okey guys, some game planning ahead on how to manage when in a trend play.  
From here on if we get on any sell trade that does fall big you want to bank but leave some of the position open... I Bank & Keep **(KB 80/20)**  
... banking 100+ for 80% and 20% of the position to run... If you catch a big trend let's say around 1000 pips... that equal to 6-7 of stop size.  
and if trending and stepping, you very well could be in multiple of it... now you are a playaa, maximizing the trend, stress free, at ease, risk free... you already have got your main chunk.  
Talking ahead this may not happen but if does you are planned for it. Being a few steps ahead helps you make _in-the-moment_ decisions with full clarity.  
I can care or less about Trend... but if it's there this is how I would play it.  
  
GL 

Stay the Course

  * [#294](/thread/post/14426352#post14426352 "Post Permalink")

  * May 16, 2023 2:31am  May 16, 2023 2:31am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

**Patience...**  
I know some of you see the wick, it looks so ripe for a drop to at least test the Valley... and you're sitting there tempted to get on this to either grab it for a quick gain or possibly be in this ride for a big drop.  
But, in reality...  
This pullback is not fully developed yet, and it could still very well reach up higher it could even be a bounce to the moon... noting is set yet.  
sit on your hands let it develop, stay patience, stay with your structure (whatever it is that you do)... stick to your plan... practice discipline... **stay the course.**  
Rides and bounces etc are everywhere... how you win with it is another story... your structure is your edge... you wanna win based on something that you can fall back on if it doesn't pan out to be the way it should've could've...  
_Structure and Risk Management_ is first and everything else 2nd the way I approach it.... you are the master or your boat tho.  
  
I see things live and find it necessary to point out, that's all... no intention to lecture by any means.  
  
GL

> Disliked
> 
> {quote} How do you feel about scaling out on stops - say taking off 33% of the trade every 10 pips against your trade?
> 
> Ignored

That would be a disaster, so the answer is no. This stop is very small and a lot of times is hit before you get to it... A lot of times just the reaction and bounce to the level travels 10-15 pips negative, so every time you would be in a winner for less amount.  
This is how you deal with stops... you lick your wound and move on to the next trade. It's part of the game.  
  
  
GL

  * [#320](/thread/post/14430513#post14430513 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 9:40am  May 19, 2023 9:20am | Edited 9:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

This should answer all your current questions about LV.  
  
The first image; price halt and continuation... that halt is just a part of the price continuation... not large enough, not long enough...  
translates to; not enough bull money inserted in order to be taken seriously. so, the LL is not level, but the peak of that small move is a Level... bcz new money did insert there to push it down further... that point is to be taken seriously.  
  
2nd image... the pullback and the resume both are fine for levels, the is price take off on both pullback and resumes.  
  
I hope it helps... just think of it; where money has showed up to push the price from any price halt!!... then, you got yourself a level there and must be tested on the next visit... some works some don't... because simply we do not know how much was inserted and if those orders still stand there later on, all we know at some point and time there was action there, that's it. But is good enough to make money from such little info anyways.  
We are served with 2nd hand info as retail traders, always remember that.  
... to counter such vulnerability, is the reason for 3R since the win rate will not be significantly high. you can hit 25% and be even money... any more than that you're profiting... but it might come and take in runs... like you will have a few losses in a row or same with wins... but its the loss one that you need to bear through, stick with it and etc, to prevail in the end and make money.

#  [](/thread/1217147-level-in-level-out)Level in Level out 

  * 

  * [#321](/thread/post/14430586#post14430586 "Post Permalink")

  * May 19, 2023 11:46am  May 19, 2023 11:46am 

  * [ pakeha](pakeha)

  * | Joined Sep 2011  | Status: Trader | [435 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=193174)

> [Quoting nadi-fx](/thread/post/14430513#post14430513 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> This should answer all your current questions about LV. The first image; price halt and continuation... that halt is just a part of the price continuation... not large enough, not long enough... translates to; not enough bull money inserted in order to be taken seriously. so, the LL is not level, but the peak of that small move is a Level... bcz new money did insert there to push it down further... that point is to be taken seriously. 2nd image... the pullback and the resume both are fine for levels, the is price take off on both pullback and resumes....
> 
> Ignored

ok, I understand the pattern(s) you have drawn. The interpretation of whether a level is formed at the lower low (in your diagram) appears to be the magnitude of the retracement, or as you call it the take off. My question remains is the determination of the magnitude of the retracement from the low a discretionary decision? Or, is there a repeatable quantitative method to confirm the take off has a high probability of creating a new level? As an example, if the takeoff from the low was greater than xx% (50%, 61.8% etc) of the downward move. Thanks. 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#322](/thread/post/14430676#post14430676 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 2:22pm  May 19, 2023 1:37pm | Edited 2:22pm 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

> [Quoting pakeha](/thread/post/14430586#post14430586 "View Quoted Post")
> 
> Disliked
> 
> {quote} ok, I understand the pattern(s) you have drawn. The interpretation of whether a level is formed at the lower low (in your diagram) appears to be the magnitude of the retracement, or as you call it the take off. My question remains is the determination of the magnitude of the retracement from the low a discretionary decision? Or, is there a repeatable quantitative method to confirm the take off has a high probability of creating a new level? As an example, if the takeoff from the low was greater than xx% (50%, 61.8% etc) of the downward...
> 
> Ignored

The reason I hesitate to use the name Retracements is because quickly gets related to Fib levels and that is not what I want here.  
I use the Take-Off bcz after the point of price halt and bounce I like to see a significant take-off and the continuation of it for some time. So, within next a few candles I need to see at least one striking one. A slow pullback means it just profit taking is taking place... a sharper pullback means profit taking + new money is coming in, now that's something I can bank on when it revisits that area again. It's like a solid wall in place and price on the revisit if not as strong will bounce off of it.  
So, No there is no discretionary decision... however as an experience trader I could tell based on strength of this current bear move that little retrace was not the highest probability level to go long from, by just looking at it. Therefore, I have come to conclusion as to how to separate/distinguish retracements... initial take off or speed or bounce or etc needs to be visible to me to validate any level... I need to see that somewhere in the first wall of the retracements.  
I don't use fib, I don't use any indicator, I don't use set of number of pips, I don't make decisions off the cuff either.  
  
I hope it helps. 

Stay the Course

> {quote} The reason I hesitate to use the name Retracements is because quickly gets related to Fib levels and that is not what I want here. ok, I get it however, the description you use need to see a significant takeoff and a continuation of it for some time means it is discretionary in other words, the determination of what is significant and some time will differ among traders. I am not saying that is a bad thing it is what it is discretionary, based on a traders personal understanding and experience in the market. The opposite of discretionary is rules-based (which can usually be coded), however for this portion of your system, rules-based doesnt apply. Not an issue for me, but needed the clarification. Cheers.

A pullback consists of a few candles on the initial leg... on those you need to see at least one of them to show strength and hold etc, (that is speed and time) ... there is nothing discretionary about that, it's very visible in the chart unless one wants to make it complicated.

Would it be better to close the buy trade or take partial profits even if its not 3R yet the moment the sell order is triggered? 

[0 ](javascript:void\(0\);) [0 ](javascript:void\(0\);)

  * [#343](/thread/post/14434933#post14434933 "Post Permalink")

  * May 24, 2023 1:40am  May 24, 2023 1:40am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

okey guys pros and cons here...  
If you BE this one you might feel good right now bcz you took a shot didn't pan out and you got away with it at no cost, which is good.  
If you are still in it like me you are risking your stop to be taken out, took a shot didn't work and will pay the price.  
  
IF this turns around and resumes the bounce to take off for a good profit or heavy one, then the upside worth more than the downside.  
  
I personally don't think about any of that, "what could happen"... I just stick to what I do every time, and that is; to play it the same every time, which is, if the position has not matured, I stick with it and gladly accept the outcome, whether is the SL or TP. 

Stay the Course

It's a choice, and that's what it...
> 
> Ignored

![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44f.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44f.png?v=15.1)![](https://resources.faireconomy.media/images/emojis/64/1f44f.png?v=15.1)

its all just one persons opinion....

  * [#384](/thread/post/14453485#post14453485 "Post Permalink")

  * Edited 3:08am  Jun 8, 2023 2:50am | Edited 3:08am 

  * [![](https://assets.faireconomy.media/nfs/customavatars/thumbs/medium/avatar968297_2.gif) nadi-fx](nadi-fx)

  * | Joined Jun 2020  | Status: Active WCT | [265 Posts](/search?do=process&provider=Member&searchuser=968297)

I see the thread quiet, and I can understand, there is no bling bling her nor should be.  
Okey so here is the story of what's happening, it is nothing short of what always happens... price makes a run then corrects for a while then makes a run corrects and so on and on...  
This time around it was a bit unfortunate since it did not give us a chance to get on ride of 450pips drop, normally it does at least once or twice to benefit from trend moves as well. This was one of the nicest clean-cut runs in some time, pullback drop pullback drop giving no DB/DT.  
what I like to hit home is this now... during the run which lasted about 3 weeks we were hit with 5 stops in a row total of -150pip... now what it seems to be is a sideway action which has already given us 3 signals, all winners... none of them were even full 3R and still has wiped all the losses, and the correction has just started... in is inside a 150 pips range up and down, how long it will last who knows... take it at face value and trade the heck out of it.  
The key is, _Patience, Staying The Course,_ just like any other successful trading style or life in general. Jumping the gun or second guessing or moving from systems to systems and else does nothing but damage and chaos to your trading career.  
Sure, you did not make money in 3 weeks, and you lost some on top of it... but trading is not clean cut, market is not clean cut, it's made of lots of twist and turns... There is not a trading method that does not go through up and downs, good runs and bad runs etc,... it all averages out in the end, but that is, **IF** you stay discipline, trust the process and stick with it, that is your only edge in this market.  
_The point is how you handle the Bear time and how you maximize the Bull time._  
When this correction lasts for couple of weeks you will make ton of money, it will recover all lost times and plenty more... but **IF** you did not go crazy during the down time, giving up more than you should have and else.  
  
Anyways I hope it makes sense.

So first post is revised...  
The big change is we got confirmation now before entering versus none before.  
in detail: you will wait for H1 candle rejection at the level before taking position.. therefore, replacing Limit orders with Stop orders  
Thats it.  
Please read the 1st post.  
  
Thx

I ended up deciding to open a new thread for the changes. The changes differ, and it's better to have its own place. I trade both ways using limit orders and go for it without confirmation when I see fit, and distinguishing between was just too much of a task to explain and display. The other thread will serve as a safer way to trade, and I thought it would fit for more people, so that is why I will be active there and keep that thread going.  
If you are interested, visit that other thread called " Level in Level out 2.0."  
  
Cheers.
